14.14.3 - Easting Comparison 
 

The sample and block model averages were calculated on 500 m composite 
sections across the easting for the Buckton Mineralized Zone (Appendix 3). Due to the 
flat nature of the deposit this is parallel to the strike of the mineralization. The purpose is 
to compare the input sample file with the resulting block model data to make sure there 
is no gross over or under estimation occurring. The easting composites generally 
compare quite well. There is some local over and under estimation observed but this is 
to be expected with the estimation process. Overall the block average grades follow the 
general trend of the input sample data. Graphs of the individual grade element 
comparisons are provided in Appendix 3.   
 
14.14.4 - Northing Comparison 

 
The input sample and block model averages were calculated on 500 m 

composite sections down the northing for the Buckton Mineralized Zone (Appendix 3). 
Due to the flat nature of the deposit this is parallel to the strike of the mineralization. The 
purpose is to compare the input sample file with the resulting block model data to make 
sure there is no gross over or under estimation occurring. The northing composites 
generally compare quite well. There is some local over and under estimation observed 
but this is to be expected with the estimation process. Overall the block averages follow 
the general trend of the input sample data. Graphs of the individual grade element 
comparisons are provided in Appendix 3.   
 



Technical Report, Buckton REE Resource Estimate, SBH Property, Northeast Alberta, Page 77 
 

 

14.15 – RESOURCE CLASSIFICATION 
 

This is a supplementary mineral resource estimate for a portion of the Buckton 
Mineralized Zone. The original Buckton maiden inferred resource estimate, which 
calculated the recoverable grades for eight metals/oxides (MoO3, Ni, U3O8, V2O5, Zn, 
Cu, Co and Li2CO3), reported 226.9 million tonnes (250.1 million short tons) at an 
average value using the recoverable metal grade and 5 year average price for the metal 
(or oxide) for all 8 metals of $USD23.0 per tonne ($US20.9 per short ton; Dufresne et 
al., 2011). This polymetallic Mo-Ni-U-V-Zn-Cu-Co-Li resource of Dufresne et al. (2011) 
remains intact. 
 

The supplementary REE-Y-Sc-Th mineral resource estimate reported here is 
complementary to the Buckton inferred maiden resource estimate of Dufresne et al. 
(2011) and is classified in accordance with guidelines established by the CIM 
"Estimation of Mineral Resources and Mineral Reserves Best Practice Guidelines" 
dated November 23

rd
, 2003 and CIM "Definition Standards for Mineral Resources and 

Mineral Reserves" dated November 14
th

, 2004. The Buckton REE-Y-Sc-Th mineral 
resource is classified as Inferred: 
 

An 'Inferred Mineral Resource' is that part of a Mineral Resource for which 
quantity and grade or quality can be estimated on the basis of geological evidence and 
limited sampling and reasonably assumed, but not verified, geological and grade 
continuity. The estimate is based on limited information and sampling gathered through 
appropriate techniques from locations such as outcrops, trenches, pits, workings and 
drill holes. 
 

Mineral resources are not mineral reserves and do not have demonstrated 
economic viability. There is no guarantee that all or any part of the inferred mineral 
resource will be converted into a mineral reserve.   
 

It is likely that not one of the metals alone at current metal prices could provide a 
stand-alone case for the economics of the Buckton Mineralized Zone. It will likely 
require several metals to create an economic deposit. In addition, the amount of 
overburden, the expected amount of recoverable metal and the price for each metal (or 
oxide) will play a critical role in the potential economics of the deposit and the final 
resource estimate. In order to evaluate this deposit as having a reasonable prospect for 
extraction it was deemed more logical and appropriate that the deposit would need to 
satisfy some minimum lower cutoff value per tonne rather than a metal equivalent lower 
grade cutoff. Based upon other ongoing resource studies for poly-metallic black shale 
hosted deposits in Sweden (Harron et al, 2008 and 2007; Puritch et al., 2010), and 
based upon a scenario of possible open pit mining of a poorly consolidated shale 
combined with heap leach processing in northeast Alberta along the eastern edge of the 
Birch Mountains upland, the location of the project with respect to access, power and 
other important infrastructure, a lower cut-off value for the mineral resource estimate of 
$USD7.5 per tonne is considered reasonable as the base case break-even point and 
lower cut-off threshold.   



Technical Report, Buckton REE Resource Estimate, SBH Property, Northeast Alberta, Page 78 
 

 

 
For the final resource estimate for the Buckton Mineralized Zone, each block and 

sub-block in the block model was assigned a cumulative $USD value based upon the 
estimated recoverable metal grade for each metal for that block, along with the $USD 
one to three year average price for that metal multiplied by the recoverable grade for 
each metal.  
 

The Buckton REE-Y-Sc-Th mineral resource estimate was calculated utilizing the 
estimated recoverable grade for each of 17 metals including REE, Y, Sc and Th. The 
estimated recoverable grade was multiplied by the one to three year average prices for 
that metal/oxide (availability pending) in $USD in order to come up with a value for each 
block and sub-block (Table 14.15). In order to evaluate the mineral resource estimate a 
lower block cut-off of $USD7.5 per tonne was employed for the estimate; the same 
estimate used in the Buckton maiden inferred resource estimate (see Dufresne et al., 
2011).  A number of recent mineral resource estimates constructed based upon open pit 
mineable and heap leachable poly-metallic black shales in Sweden have employed 
$USD7.5 per tonne as the break-even point and lower cut-off (Harron et al., 2009, 2008 
and 2007; Puritch et al., 2010). Based upon a scenario of possible open pit mining 
combined with heap leaching in northeast Alberta along the eastern edge of the Birch 
Mountains, with potential for a low strip ratio at startup, the likely free-dig nature of the 
SWS shale, the potential for easy access to multiple working faces, the location of the 
project with respect to access, power and other important infrastructure, the lower cut-
off value of $US7.5 per tonne for the mineral resource estimate was considered 
reasonable. Lastly, the lower cut-off value of $US7.5 per tonne estimates production for 
the traditional metals plus REE-Y-Sc-Th as a pregnant solution co-product, but it is 
unclear what additional costs will be incurred to extract and refine the REE-Y-Sc-Th 
metals into a saleable product. Although we provide recoverable grades and an 
estimated value per tonne, there is much less confidence in the long term REE pricing, 
the long term viability of REE supply, what effects new production will have on REE 
pricing, the actual cost of extracting the REE's from a pregnant polymetallic solution. 
 

The Buckton mineral resource was classified using the $USD7.5 per tonne lower 
cut-off versus depth for each block from surface with a separate table of resources for 
blocks within 25 m, 50 m, 75 m, 100 m and 125 m of surface topography (Table 14.15). 
The final reported resource based on what is believed to have a reasonable prospect for 
extraction in the future is based upon blocks within 75 m of surface and using a lower 
cut-off of $USD7.50 per tonne.  
 

The mineral resource is classified as inferred based upon the CIM Guidelines 
and consists of 226.9 million tonnes (250.1 million short tons) at an average value using 
the recoverable metal grade and one- to three-year average prices for the metal (or 
oxide) for the total rare earth oxides (REO) plus Y2O3 of $USD22.00 per tonne 
($US20.00 per short ton) as displayed in Tables 14.15 and 14.16. The total REO,Y2O3 
raw grade is 320 ppm. If Sc2O3 and ThO2 are added, the total 17 element resource 
becomes $USD57.73 per tonne ($US52.37 per short ton). 
 



Technical Report, Buckton REE Resource Estimate, SBH Property, Northeast Alberta, Page 79 
 

 

This REE-Y-Sc-Th-focused mineral resource estimate has been classified as 
inferred according to the CIM definition standards.  This classification is based on a 
number of factors which are noted below: 
 

 Limited number of drill holes making up this resource. 

 Wide spaced nature of the drilling. 
 Good continuity of mineralization and geological control from section to section 

along 6 km of strike.  
 additional metallurgical work required additional assessment of co-products 

complementary to the original Buckton inferred maiden resource estimate of 
Dufresne et al. (2011). 

 
Plan views of the Buckton Mineralized Zone block model with attached values per 

tonne based upon recoverable metal (or oxide), the one to three year average price of 
the metal (or oxide) and meeting thresholds of $USD7.5 per tonne for blocks within 25 
m, 50 m, 75 m, 100 m, 125 m and 150 m of surface topography are presented in 
Figures 14.6 to 14.11. 
 

This is a supplementary inferred maiden mineral resource estimate for the Buckton 
Mineralized Zone and the SBH Property. The original Buckton inferred maiden resource 
estimate of Dufresne et al. (2011) remains intact (226.9 million tonnes at $USD23.0 per 
tonne for MoO3, Ni, U3O8, V2O5, Zn, Cu, Co).  
 
 
15. ADJACENT PROPERTIES  
 

The northern boundary of DNI's SBH Property is adjacent to mineral permits held 
by Athabasca Minerals Inc. (Athabasca) of Edmonton, Alberta. Athabasca currently 
holds total MAIM Permits totalling more than 491,727 ha in the Fort McMurray region of 
northeast Alberta. They are currently engaged in exploration for industrial minerals such 
as silica sand, limestone, salt, and aggregate. 
 
 

To the immediate east of the SBH Property are mineral permits operated by the 
Hammerstone Corporation (Hammerstone). Hammerstone is actively engaged in 
exploration for industrial minerals on its northern Alberta properties, in particular 
aggregate and limestone resources.  
 

There are no known mineral resources or significant mineral discoveries on these 
properties. 



Technical Report, Buckton REE Resource Estimate, SBH Property, Northeast Alberta, Page 80

16. OTHER RELEVANT DATA AND INFORMATION 
 

This is the supplementary independent mineral resource estimate prepared for 
DNI's Buckton Mineralized Zone with emphasis on additional assessment of co-
products complementary to the original Buckton inferred maiden resource estimate of 
Dufresne et al. (2011), which remains intact (226.9 million tonnes at $USD23.0 per 
tonne for MoO3, Ni, U3O8, V2O5, Zn, Cu, Co). 
 

This technical report provides the resource for the recoverable REE, Y, Sc and 
Th. Any REE's produced would be a "free and clear" co-product from mining through to 
solution stage refinement. Although recoverable grades and an estimated value per 
tonne is provided in this Technical Report, there is much less confidence in long term 
REE pricing, the long term REE viability of supply, what effects new production will have 
on REE pricing, the actual cost of separating individual REE's from pregnant 
polymetallic solution, and getting the extracted metals into a useable or saleable form. 
These concerns are shared by all other REE projects.  
 
 
17. INTERPRETATION AND CONCLUSIONS 
 

DNI Metal Inc.'s SBH Property is located, approximately 120 km north of Fort 
McMurray, Alberta in the Birch Mountains. The Property consists of 272,032 hectares 
(ha) in 36 contiguous Permits that are held 100% by DNI. The primary exploration target 
on the SBH Property is poly-metallic metal zones hosted in mid-Cretaceous Second 
White Specks black shale. The poly-metallic zones extend over vast areas (100's of 
km

2
), occurring in flat-lying near-surface stratigraphy that may be amenable to 

extraction by open pit bulk mining methods where overburden strip ratios are sufficiently 
low to allow economic extraction. Several poly-metallic zones have been identified 
within DNI's Property by historic exploration, two of which have been confirmed by 
historic drilling. The primary targets are the Buckton Mineralized Zone and the Asphalt 
Mineralized Zone both of which are known to be near surface, laterally extensive and 
are partly exposed along the eastern and southern edge of the Birch Mountains. The 
Property's large size is appropriate to the type and size of poly-metallic targets being 
sought by DNI.  
 

The polymetallic Mo-Ni-U-V-Zn-Cu-Co-Li resource of Dufresne et al. (2011; i.e., 
Buckton inferred maiden resource estimate) remains the fundamental maiden resource 
estimate for a portion of DNI's Buckton Mineralized Zone and consisted of 226.9 million 
tonnes at $USD23.0 per tonne. This supplementary independent mineral resource 
estimate for DNI's Buckton Mineralized Zone has been prepared in support of a recent 
DNI press release that discloses positive bioleach extraction results for liberating rare 
earth elements (REE) and other specialty metals from the Second White Speckled 
Shale Formation in northeastern Alberta (DNI Metals Inc., Press Release, September 8, 
2011). Despite there being no additional drilling at the Buckton Mineralized Zone, the 



Technical Report, Buckton REE Resource Estimate, SBH Property, Northeast Alberta, Page 89 
 

 

additional metallurgical work requires additional assessment of co-products to 
complement and assess the full potential of this large, low-grade polymetallic resource  
 

The REE, Y, Sc and Th mineral resource model and estimate was prepared by 
Mr. Roy Eccles, P.Geol. and Mr. Steve Nicholls, MAIG under the direction and 
supervision of Mr. Dufresne. The model was generated using the combined drillhole 
data derived from the 1997 and 2011 drilling campaigns. Modeling was constrained by 
the formational boundaries of the Second White Specks Shale. Domains were 
interpreted that reflect distinct zones or types of poly-metallic mineralization. 
Interpolation characteristics in the resource model were defined based on the geology, 
drill hole spacing and geostatistical analysis of the data contained within these domains. 
Mineral resources were classified in accordance with guidelines established by the 
Canadian Institute of Mining, Metallurgy and Petroleum (CIM) "Estimation of Mineral 
Resources and Mineral Reserves Best Practice Guidelines" dated November 23

rd
, 2003 

and CIM "Definition Standards for Mineral Resources and Mineral Reserves" dated 
November 27

th
, 2010.  

 
The Buckton Zone mineral resource modeling and estimation was carried out 

using a 3-dimensional block model based on geostatistical applications using 
commercial mine planning software MICROMINE (v12.0.4). A total of eight diamond 
drillholes were used in the resource estimate.  Spacing between drill holes varies from 
240 m to 2.5 km, with an average distance of about 1 km between drillholes. There are 
four drill sections that range in spacing from about 670 m to 2 km between sections. 
The REE sample file comprised 549 samples of variable length from all lithologies but 
when composited in MICROMINE yielded a database of 302 sample composites that 
were used for the mineral resource estimate. Data supplied and utilized in MICROMINE 
included collar easting, northing and elevation coordinates, lithology, along with assay 
data for REE, Y, Sc and Th, as well as bulk density (specific gravity) data.  All drillholes 
were drilled vertically and as such there was no down hole survey information collected.  
 

Variography was conducted on the composited drillhole data within the Second 
White Specks Shale domain to produce spherical semi variograms. Each element was 
modeled individually to determine the continuity and orientation of mineralization.  As a 
result of the wide drillhole spacing's a parent model block size of 250 m x 250 m x 2 m 
was chosen for the Buckton block modeling and resource estimate.  Sub-blocking was 
conducted down to 25 m x 25 m x 1 m.  The block model was extended far enough past 
the mineralized wireframe to encompass the entire mineralized shale domain.  
 

The Buckton Zone REE-Y-Sc-Th mineral resource estimate has been calculated 
utilizing the estimated recoverable grade for each of 17 metals (or oxides thereof) 
including the REE, Y, Sc and Th.  The estimated recoverable grade was derived from 
multiplying the raw estimated grades by the estimated recovery percentages based 
upon metallurgical test work completed to date (Table 17.1).  The poly-metallic 
recoverable grades were translated into a $USD value for each block and sub-block by 
multiplying the one- to three-year average price for that metal in $USD in order to 
evaluate the mineral resource estimate (Table 17.1). In order to economically evaluate 



Technical Report, Buckton REE Resource Estimate, SBH Property, Northeast Alberta, Page 90 
 

 

the mineral resource estimate a lower block value cut-off of $USD7.5 per tonne was 
employed for the estimate.  A number of recent mineral resource estimates constructed 
based upon open pit mineable, heap leachable, poly-metallic black shales in Sweden 
have employed a $USD7.5 per tonne as the break-even point and lower economic cut-
off (Harron et al, 2008 and 2007; Puritch et al., 2010). Based upon a scenario of 
possible open pit mining combined with heap leaching in northeast Alberta along the 
eastern edge of the Birch Mountains upland, the location of the project with respect to 
access, power and other important infrastructure, a lower cut-off value for the mineral 
resource estimate of $USD7.5 per tonne is considered reasonable as the base case 
lower cut-off threshold.  The Second White Specks Shale at the edge of the Birch 
Mountains upland forms a relatively continuous horizontal zone with a favourable 
configuration with respect to open pit mining.  
 

The final reported resource is based on what is believed to have a reasonable 
prospect for extraction in the future given the current open pit mining parameters that 
exist for northeast Alberta. The preferred final mineral resource estimate utilizes blocks 
within 75 m of surface and a lower cut-off of $USD7.5 per tonne (Table 17.1).  
 

The mineral resource is classified as inferred based upon the CIM Guidelines 
and consists of 226.9 million tonnes (250.1 million short tons) at an average value using 
the recoverable metal grade and one- to three-year average prices for the metal (or 
oxide) for the total rare earth oxides (REO) plus Y2O3 of $USD22.00 per tonne 
($US20.00 per short ton) as displayed in Table 17.1. The total REO,Y2O3 raw grade is 
320 ppm. If Sc2O3 and ThO2 are added, the total 17 element resource becomes 
$USD57.73 per tonne ($US52.37 per short ton). 
 

Lastly, we show that the REE-enriched Second White Speckled Shale could 
have a similar paragenesis as the REE ion-adsorption clay deposits in southern China. 
Scanning electron microprobe test work on the Second White Specks shale suggests 
shows that metals of interest occur as charged particles within oxides, hydroxides and 

-
Lu,Y and P/Al, in combination with the negative Ce anomaly (oxidizing conditions) and 
sulphide, provide additional evidence that precipitation of oxyhydroxides occurred within 
the REE-enriched layers. Accepting that the Second White Speckled Shale in the SBH 
Property area was influenced by hydrothermal events, the lack of any Eu chondrite-
normalized anomaly suggests trivalent Eu associated with low temperature fluids. 
Lastly, the Second White Speckled Shale has similar MREE-enriched PAAS-normalized 
REE profiles and total REO (0.03 wt. %) as the Chinese ion-adsorption REE deposits 
(e.g., Longnan deposit in China comprises 0.03-0.35 wt. % total REO). The analogy 
between the Second White Speckled Shale and ion-adsorption clay deposits in 
southern China is important because the ion-adsorption deposits are exploited 
economically because it is relatively easy to extract REE.  
 
 
 
 



Technical Report, Buckton REE Resource Estimate, SBH Property, Northeast Alberta, Page 91

18. RECOMMENDATIONS 
 

Recommendations for 2012 exploration include, but are not limited to, three 
fundamental areas for advancement of DNI's SBH Property. The total cost of the 
recommended exploration is approximately CDN$9 million.  

 
First, the Buckton Mineralized Zone has excellent potential for expansion. Based 

on exploration conducted to date, the authors recommend that the following work be 
completed at the SBH Property and the Buckton Mineralized Zone during 2012.  
 

1. Step out resource drilling to expand the current Inferred Resource immediately 
north and northeast of drillhole 7BK05, where no drilling exists. Drilling to the 
north will also test theories of whether high-grade shale continues and even 
increases in metal content in this direction;  
 

2. Step out drilling to the northeast and southeast along the erosional edge of the 
Birch Mountains to test overburden thickness and locate areas where metal 
grades to strip ratios establish high priority areas of feasibility, and 

 
3. Infill drilling in and around drillholes 7BK04, 7BK05 and 11BK01 to 11BK05 to 

provide greater confidence in the continuity, particularly the continuity of the 
thickness of the Second White Specks Shale. The infill drilling will also enable 
DNI to convert some or all of the existing Inferred Resource to a higher Resource 
Category. 

 
4. To provide additional Second White Specks Shale material for bench scale 

metallurgical leach studies, 
 

The proposed drill program for 2012 should include approximately 5,000 m of 
diamond drilling in approximately 40 holes. The expected drilling cost for either 
helicopter supported fall drilling or winter road accessible drilling is an average all-in 
cost of $1,000/m for a total cost of CDN$5.0 million. 
 

Secondly, potential analogies between the REE-enriched Second White 
Speckled Shale and REE ion-adsorption clay deposits in southern China are important 
because extraction of REE from ion-adsorption deposits is a relatively straightforward 
process in comparison to other traditional rock-hosted REE deposit sources. Continued 
metallurgical assessment including bench scale bulk sample leaching work, is 
considered critical to assess the extractability of the metals on potential leach pads, and 
assessing potential metal residence/extraction times and reagent consumption. In 
addition, test work should be initiated on REO recovery from the pregnant liquor right 
through to refining the REO concentrate into a final REE product. Mineralogical, 
metallurgical test work estimated at a total cost of about CDN$1.5 million. 
 

Lastly, DNI's SBH Property has considerable potential for hosting large quantities 
of metals in near-surface Second White Specks Shale black shale zones. In addition to 



Technical Report, Buckton REE Resource Estimate, SBH Property, Northeast Alberta, Page 93 
 

 

the Buckton Mineralized Zone, a number of other targets areas, including the Buckton 
South and Ashton mineralized zones have excellent exploration potential. Further 
consideration should be given to drilling poly-metallic exploration targets at Buckton 
South and Ashton mineralized zones. Using the average all-in drilling cost of $1,000/m, 
20 holes (approximately 2,500 m) would cost approximately CDN$2.5 million.                                   
 
 
 
 
 
      APEX Geoscience Ltd. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
       

D. Roy Eccles, M.Sc., P.Geol.
